<span id="freeTextContainer17928460388993675330">You wonder how many more varieties of driven, murderous teen girls Megan Abbott can come up with. She's already covered the obvious trifecta - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1760404182' title='My review of You Will Know Me' rel='nofollow noopener'>gymnasts,</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1365826542' title='My review of Dare Me' rel='nofollow noopener'>cheerleaders</a> and, um, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/944966221' title='My review of The Fever' rel='nofollow noopener'>witches</a> - and now she's on to...science nerds? What's next?<br/><br/><b>Intense Teens Who Might Still Murder Somebody</b><br/>- Theater girls<br/>- Girls who just became vegetarians <br/>- A cappella singers<br/>- Yearbook editors<br/><br/>The reason Megan Abbott is (slightly) less famous than, like, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1592022250' title='My review of Dark Places' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gillian Flynn</a> is, she doesn't have the flair for big twists. She's won</span>
  <span id="freeText17928460388993675330" style="display:none">You wonder how many more varieties of driven, murderous teen girls Megan Abbott can come up with. She's already covered the obvious trifecta - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1760404182" title="My review of You Will Know Me" rel="nofollow noopener">gymnasts,</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1365826542" title="My review of Dare Me" rel="nofollow noopener">cheerleaders</a> and, um, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/944966221" title="My review of The Fever" rel="nofollow noopener">witches</a> - and now she's on to...science nerds? What's next?<br /><br /><b>Intense Teens Who Might Still Murder Somebody</b><br />- Theater girls<br />- Girls who just became vegetarians <br />- A cappella singers<br />- Yearbook editors<br /><br />The reason Megan Abbott is (slightly) less famous than, like, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1592022250" title="My review of Dark Places" rel="nofollow noopener">Gillian Flynn</a> is, she doesn't have the flair for big twists. She's wonderful at characters, mood, tone and pacing, but you want more murdering. There are usually only like two suspects. Sometimes there's barely a crime at all. The big twist in the one about witches is that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[they aren't witches, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> which, I mean, first of all, says who.<br /><br />But she's getting better! And this one's very good. It's got more blood, for one thing - the body count is higher. And its villain, angular Diane Fleming, might be Abbott's best character yet. All pretty and shy and science-y, and...<b>
  <i>evil?</i>
</b><br /><br />Abbott is my favorite writer working today, sorry <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1942410344" title="My review of Half of a Yellow Sun" rel="nofollow noopener">Chimamanda Adichie</a> but you could have murderous teens too you know - and she's at the height of her game right now. For me, personally, we're getting closer and closer to the girls I personally dated during high school, so once we get to Murderous Teen Members of the Amnesty International Club we'll be inside my life and will we even be able to count the bodies?</span>

<div id="review_2177719740" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2177719740" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38727943-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451400366p2/38727943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177719740?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/38727943-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38727943-jenna?shelf=academia-and-college-campus">academia-and-college-campus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38727943-jenna?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38727943-jenna?shelf=workplace-drama">workplace-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38727943-jenna?shelf=crossed-over-to-the-dark-side">crossed-over-to-the-dark-side</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38727943-jenna?shelf=bad-teachers-or-students">bad-teachers-or-students</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38727943-jenna?shelf=2018-reading-challenge">2018-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38727943-jenna?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38727943-jenna?shelf=boarding-school-camp-or-high-school">boarding-school-camp-or-high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38727943-jenna?shelf=gothic-novel">gothic-novel</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177719740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15506023758592290086">Are you...crying?! There’s no crying in...science!<br/>There might be murder, though.<br/><br/>I feel like Megan Abbott is sort of the Tom Hanks of thrillers. Everyone pretty much seems to love her, and deservedly so; her talent is pretty much consistently unimpeachable, more or less a safe and sure bet. Here she’s given us another totally solid book, which for me fell somewhere between a completely respectable 3 and 4 stars. (A Lab of Their Own?? sorry, couldn’t resist...).<br/><br/>I do think it’s a fair observation t</span>
  <span id="freeText15506023758592290086" style="display:none">Are you...crying?! There’s no crying in...science!<br />There might be murder, though.<br /><br />I feel like Megan Abbott is sort of the Tom Hanks of thrillers. Everyone pretty much seems to love her, and deservedly so; her talent is pretty much consistently unimpeachable, more or less a safe and sure bet. Here she’s given us another totally solid book, which for me fell somewhere between a completely respectable 3 and 4 stars. (A Lab of Their Own?? sorry, couldn’t resist...).<br /><br />I do think it’s a fair observation that Abbott’s books - except for one, but I’ll get back to that - follow a certain template and can be a bit predictable by this point, especially if you’ve already put away a few of them in the past. I will admit that at times, a certain weary sense of deja vu descended upon me like a formaldehyde cloud and made me feel as though this book and I were lacking a certain - wait for it... - chemistry! (bahahah!)<br /><br />That being said, there were a few things I especially appreciated about this book that set it apart from some of its predecessors. For one, I thought the traditionally male dominated science lab setting was pretty spectacular, even better than the worlds of competitive cheerleading and gymnastics and adding extra layers of complexity and nuance. A ruthless STEM ambition murder mystery? - I am here for that!*<br /><br />I also thought Diane was a much more interesting antagonist than in many of Abbott’s previous books, especially that of You Will Know Me. I loved Abbott’s turn away from a more “mean girl” type of villainess toward a more quiet and mysterious, conflicted, otherworldly antihero. I also loved the inclusion of PMDD as a possible risk factor for the...let’s say Megan Abbotty types of things that take place in the novel - although I will say that I think perhaps a little more could have been done with this. And did anyone else find that this book seemed a lot more bloody/gruesome and gothic even than typical Abbott??<br /><br />In all, I think this book represents fully matured, classic Megan Abbott. Don’t get me wrong - the prose still walks that edgy noir line and sometimes teeters a bit into the over-the-topness that we’ve clearly grown to know and love. But this one never really falters into sounding like ... a parody of Megan Abbott.<br /><br />As for the book I mentioned earlier that seems to be somewhat of an outlier in the Abbott oeuvre - shout out to The Fever! This is my FAVORITE Abbott book by far, and one of my favorite novels as well. I know many people don’t feel this way, but if you love this book - I’m with you!!<br /><br />* I REALLY wanted to title this review “Dial STEM For Murder!” - but I thought, that’s so good that surely someone’s thought of it already. So I Googled it and sure enough, at least one British news site seems to have used it (for an article about a school science class studying a fake crime scene at a sewage plant, whaaat). Good try, though, right?!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15506023758592290086" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1108056-josh?shelf=own">own</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2489638373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer870975072379844872">Megan Abbot has a wonderful ability to convey the inner most desires of her characters in a way which feels like the reader is peaking beneath a curtain into the watery pools of their emotions.<br/><br/>Give Me Your Hand is noir without the sepia splash and minus the mysterious fedora-wearing character. In their place are test tubes, lab mice, and vibrant characters full of life who are bursting at the seams with secrets and ambition. <br/><br/>Under a microscope, Kit Owens and Diane Fleming share a thirst for scie</span>
  <span id="freeText870975072379844872" style="display:none">Megan Abbot has a wonderful ability to convey the inner most desires of her characters in a way which feels like the reader is peaking beneath a curtain into the watery pools of their emotions.<br /><br />Give Me Your Hand is noir without the sepia splash and minus the mysterious fedora-wearing character. In their place are test tubes, lab mice, and vibrant characters full of life who are bursting at the seams with secrets and ambition. <br /><br />Under a microscope, Kit Owens and Diane Fleming share a thirst for science; a lust for knowledge, and a need to become someone. They also share a secret which plagues both from their formative years of teenage angst through to their professional place in the world of pharmaceuticals.<br /><br />A secret worth killing to keep. <br /><br />My rating: 5/5 stars. Megan Abbott has crafted a tension-filled novel that threatens to boil at any moment, each chapter threatens the status quo. These character are dangerous and are portrayed as such.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2481153765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17683509619515729020">3.5 emotionally charged stars<br/><br/>“Nothing is more creative... nor destructive... than a brilliant mind with a purpose.” (Dan Brown)<br/><br/>There is a lot to be said about brilliant minds and the need to be the very best. One can give up everything to achieve the awards, the scholarships, the accolades, and the recognition they so desire. One can even give up a life to pursue their ends. Meet Kit Owens and Diane Fleming two intense girls brought together in Megan Abbott's Give Me Your Hand.<br/><br/> They meet in high</span>
  <span id="freeText17683509619515729020" style="display:none">3.5 emotionally charged stars<br /><br />“Nothing is more creative... nor destructive... than a brilliant mind with a purpose.” (Dan Brown)<br /><br />There is a lot to be said about brilliant minds and the need to be the very best. One can give up everything to achieve the awards, the scholarships, the accolades, and the recognition they so desire. One can even give up a life to pursue their ends. Meet Kit Owens and Diane Fleming two intense girls brought together in Megan Abbott's Give Me Your Hand.<br /><br /> They meet in high school, each a competitor, one spurring the other on, until a secret is revealed and their lives drift apart. They both go their separate ways for years, each achieving lofty standards until fate and a brilliant research scientist bring them together once again to compete for a spot on her team investigating the effects of premenstrual rage that at times plagues women. Kit knows a terrible secret about her one time friend and yet has never revealed it. Why has she held this unrevealed secret for so long and will she get to use it as both she and Diane vie for a spot on the team? How far does one go to get where they want to be? <br /><br />This was quite the intense story of how a secret effects the life of both the giver and the receiver of the secret's history. Secrets reveal the mind and the heart of the girls in this tale and as the time draws near for the selection of the team, both girls, now grown to women, twist and turn to achieve what they want. Lives are in danger and lives can be lost yet, to get what you want is there really anything you would not do to achieve that goal?<br /><br />This was definitely a book that presented a side of brilliant minds that was devious, cunning, and frightening. Can brilliance breed insanity? It’s a fine line separating intelligence and insanity. Will these girls cross that line or have they already done so? <br /><br />My reviews can be found here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://yayareadslotsofbooks.wordpress.com/">https://yayareadslotsofbooks.wordpres...</a><br /><br />Thanks once again to my local library for purchasing a copy of this intense novel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17683509619515729020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2277175500" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2277175500" />
    <a title="Kristy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/126296-kristy"><img alt="Kristy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489592689p2/126296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2277175500?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristy" href="/user/show/126296-kristy">Kristy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316547185" href="/book/show/35959737-give-me-your-hand">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126296-kristy?shelf=a-real-book-wow">a-real-book-wow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126296-kristy?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126296-kristy?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126296-kristy?shelf=from-the-library">from-the-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126296-kristy?shelf=little-brown">little-brown</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126296-kristy?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2277175500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6070497629849434853">Kit Owens is surviving high school but not living up to her true potential when Diane Fleming arrives at her school. Diane awakens a fire in Kit and the two form an unlikely friendship that propels Kit to academic success in her senior year. She and Diane study together and push each other to reach to be the best. Kit can't help but feel bad for her friend, who lives with her grandfather after the death of her dad. But all that changes when Diane shares an explosive secret with Kit, one that cha</span>
  <span id="freeText6070497629849434853" style="display:none">Kit Owens is surviving high school but not living up to her true potential when Diane Fleming arrives at her school. Diane awakens a fire in Kit and the two form an unlikely friendship that propels Kit to academic success in her senior year. She and Diane study together and push each other to reach to be the best. Kit can't help but feel bad for her friend, who lives with her grandfather after the death of her dad. But all that changes when Diane shares an explosive secret with Kit, one that changes the way she views Diane and basically ends their friendship. Ten years later, Kit has tried to put Diane (and her secret) behind her. She's working in the lab of a female scientist, Dr. Severin, whom she's idolized for years--a woman Diane first helped introduce her to. But when Dr. Severin earns a prestigious grant and Kit learns that Diane is suddenly in the running for one of the coveted spots to work with the Doctor on the research, the past comes rushing back. Soon Diane and Kit find themselves over their head, with secrets and horror lurking around every corner. <br /><br />So, <i>I wasn't sure I was going to enjoy this one as I started it, but it grew on me</i>. It's not really a pleasant read, at all, and none of the characters are ones you'll really love, but <i>it's very compelling and there's a slow, foreboding creepiness that keeps you reading</i>. I read this one quickly, as <i>it's dark, twisty, and intense and very easy-to-read</i> (as in, a page-turner, not the subject matter). <br /><br /><i>
  <b>"My mom always say, you don't have a self until you have a secret." ~Diane</b>
</i> <br /><br />The novel flips between the "then" and "now" format, with Kit narrating to us. It's a female-centered book, and it easily depicts women's uphill battle in the workplace. It also shows the complicated feelings of our female characters: Kit has a lot of thoughts. Her struggle from a poor high school student to doctor is a fascinating one, even if I found her hard to empathize with. <i>You won't necessarily agree with a lot of these characters' (sometimes outlandish) choices, but you'll find them oddly fascinating</i>. I enjoyed how the novel delved into the darkness of friendship--and some of the competition that can come with it. Diane and Kit's relationship is dark and intense, as is the entire novel, really. <i>The secrets that layer this book unravel slowly and eerily, and it really does keep you reading.</i> <br /><br />I especially thought this one was redeemed or bolstered by its ending; often a thriller is so good and then deflates at the end, but I actually thought this one got a little better at the end. <i>The ending is really well-done, and I didn't feel let down whatsoever. </i><br /><br /><i>Overall, this is a dark, intense, and compelling psychological thriller.</i> It's not exactly packed with loveable characters, but they are flawed, interesting, and--at times--quite creepy. <i>You'll be drawn in by its twisty plot and complicated portrayal of friendship and secrets.</i> 3.75 - 4 stars. <br /><br /><a href="http://justacatandabookatherside.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/mwcmoto" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.facebook.com/justacatandabook/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> ~ <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/+KristyHamiltonbooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/mwcmoto/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6070497629849434853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2500205925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2500205925" />
    <a title="Amanda - Mrs B&#39;s Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16323644-amanda---mrs-b-s-book-reviews"><img alt="Amanda - Mrs B&#39;s Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475233170p2/16323644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2500205925?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda - Mrs B&#39;s Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda - Mrs B&#39;s Book Reviews" href="/user/show/16323644-amanda---mrs-b-s-book-reviews">Amanda - Mrs B&#39;s Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16323644-amanda---mrs-b-s-book-reviews?shelf=review-book">review-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16323644-amanda---mrs-b-s-book-reviews?shelf=2018-books">2018-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2500205925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12829736218970266343">*<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://mrsbbookreviews.wordpress.com'>https://mrsbbookreviews.wordpress.com</a><br/>Megan Abbott is the award winning author behind the novel Give Me Your Hand. Abbott’s niche is noir fiction. Give Me Your Hand is a prime example of a chilling psychological thriller. With a dramatic shattered glass style front cover, there is an ominous tone to this novel, before you have even read the first sentence. Give Me Your Hand centres on two strong female protagonists, Diane and Kit, who were best friends in high school. A rift formed between Diane</span>
  <span id="freeText12829736218970266343" style="display:none">*<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://mrsbbookreviews.wordpress.com">https://mrsbbookreviews.wordpress.com</a><br />Megan Abbott is the award winning author behind the novel Give Me Your Hand. Abbott’s niche is noir fiction. Give Me Your Hand is a prime example of a chilling psychological thriller. With a dramatic shattered glass style front cover, there is an ominous tone to this novel, before you have even read the first sentence. Give Me Your Hand centres on two strong female protagonists, Diane and Kit, who were best friends in high school. A rift formed between Diane and Kit so deep that it has fractured their relationship. Years later, both these highly intelligent and ambitious women will battle it out to reign supreme. What follows is a story of sacrifice, determination, rivalry, jealously, bitterness, secrets and bloodshed. Abbott’s novel has received plenty of praise from fellow authors and has been well received by reviewers across all social media platforms. This is my first experience of Megan Abbott’s writing, I found her prose slick and clear. There were some instances in the lab based sections of the storyline that I felt went way over my head, so you need a good clear mind for these parts. The narrative itself was slow to begin, but revved up in the second half, complete with a full throttle conclusion I didn’t see coming. The characters are hard to develop any sense of empathy towards, but they are intriguing and well placed. The primary protagonists offer a good example of highly ambitious women, who are trying to gain the upper hand in a professional male dominated world. Full appreciation goes to the author, Megan Abbott, for putting the spotlight on women in this situation. I recommend Give Me Your Hand to thriller fans.<br /><br />*I wish to thank Pan Macmillan for providing me with a free copy of this book for review purposes.<br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12829736218970266343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2610119095" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2610119095" />
    <a title="Darinda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5465462-darinda"><img alt="Darinda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512023863p2/5465462.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2610119095?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darinda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darinda" href="/user/show/5465462-darinda">Darinda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316547185" href="/book/show/35959737-give-me-your-hand">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5465462-darinda?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2610119095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11776082341235272886">Kit and Diane were best friends in high school, until Diane told Kit a disturbing secret one day. Now, 10 years later, the two women are vying for a coveted position on a special project in a research lab. Kit is not pleased to see Diane. When Diane finds out a secret about Kit, things become even more complicated.<br/><br/>The story of what happened between Kit and Diane unfolds with alternate timelines. The "Then" is when they were teenagers, best friends with ambitious futures in science. The "Now" is </span>
  <span id="freeText11776082341235272886" style="display:none">Kit and Diane were best friends in high school, until Diane told Kit a disturbing secret one day. Now, 10 years later, the two women are vying for a coveted position on a special project in a research lab. Kit is not pleased to see Diane. When Diane finds out a secret about Kit, things become even more complicated.<br /><br />The story of what happened between Kit and Diane unfolds with alternate timelines. The "Then" is when they were teenagers, best friends with ambitious futures in science. The "Now" is when they are working in research, and competing for a position on the same research team.<br /><br />Kit and Diane share some similarities, mainly that they are both very intelligent, ambitious, and driven women. Kit has dreamed of a career in research, and has high hopes of landing a position on a groundbreaking project. Unexpectedly, Diane shows up and is hired to work in the same research lab, and along with her appearance comes memories Kit had put behind her.<br /><br />The research lab has a small group of people whom Kit has been working with, and developed good working relationships. The leader of the project is an equally ambitious woman, but the other team members are all men. The newly funded project deals with premenstrual dysphoric disorder (PMDD), and the men seem to think Kit is a shoo-in for the project because she is a woman. When Diane shows up, the work dynamic is changed, and no one is sure who the other person chosen for the team will be... which increases tension in the lab.<br /><br />This was an entertaining read, and I especially enjoyed that a good portion of the story deals with science and research. I also like the strong, but flawed, women characters. The story has some intriguing and intense parts, but also fell flat. I was expecting to be gripped by this book, but it never really captured me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11776082341235272886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ldQsv6/3FsUQLg2plcWOUSyGw+w5OqQNJNztEeZduhexWy/QNXI1vejON5LGvLI0Xl6JukdcMY21nZa3DHGNHw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('heE3A3V0ywKKbhiM4rRcZ/zv6OmGy/0A9KQBuCxkEKuhbjRs7/HoenKOIrexzWACjjeiv/itaIBl5Xoexkgnow==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8896299940803251832">Megan Abbott is the Edgar®-winning author of the novels Die a Little, Queenpin, The Song Is You, Bury Me Deep, The End of Everything, Dare Me, The Fever, You Will Know Me and Give Me Your Hand.<br/><br/>Abbott is co-showrunner, writer and executive producer of DARE ME, the TV show adapated from her novel. She was also a staff writer on HBO's THE DEUCE. Her writing has also appeared in the New York Times, th</span>
  <span id="freeText8896299940803251832" style="display:none">Megan Abbott is the Edgar®-winning author of the novels Die a Little, Queenpin, The Song Is You, Bury Me Deep, The End of Everything, Dare Me, The Fever, You Will Know Me and Give Me Your Hand.<br /><br />Abbott is co-showrunner, writer and executive producer of DARE ME, the TV show adapated from her novel. She was also a staff writer on HBO's THE DEUCE. Her writing has also appeared in the New York Times, the Guardian, Wall Street Journal, the Los Angeles Times Magazine, The Believer and the Los Angeles Review of Books.<br /><br />Born in the Detroit area, she graduated from the University of Michigan and received her Ph.D. in English and American literature from New York University. She has taught at NYU, SUNY and the New School University and has served as the John Grisham Writer in Residence at The University of Mississippi.<br /><br />She is also the author of a nonfiction book, The Street Was Mine: White Masculinity in Hardboiled Fiction and Film Noir, and the editor of A Hell of a Woman, an anthology of female crime fiction. She is currently developing two of her novels, Dare Me and The Fever, for television.</span>
